<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Guinea" title="Economy of Guinea">Economy of Guinea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg/350px-Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg" width="350" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg/525px-Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg/700px-Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2668" data-file-height="2085" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A proportional depiction of Guinea's export products.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea,_Africa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea%2C_Africa.jpg/250px-Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea%2C_Africa.jpg" width="250" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea%2C_Africa.jpg/375px-Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea%2C_Africa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea%2C_Africa.jpg/500px-Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea%2C_Africa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2828" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fisher_women_on_River_Niger_in_Guinea,_Africa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Malinke fisher women on the Niger River, <a href="/wiki/Niandankoro" title="Niandankoro">Niandankoro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kankan_Region" title="Kankan Region">Kankan Region</a>, in eastern Guinea.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Guinea has abundant natural resources including 25 percent or more of the world's known <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a> reserves. Guinea also has diamonds, gold, and other metals. The country has great potential for <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_power" title="Hydroelectric power" class="mw-redirect">hydroelectric power</a>. Bauxite and alumina are currently the only major exports. Other industries include processing plants for beer, juices, soft drinks and tobacco. Agriculture employs 80 percent of the nation's labor force. Under French rule, and at the beginning of independence, Guinea was a major exporter of bananas, <a href="/wiki/Pineapples" title="Pineapples" class="mw-redirect">pineapples</a>, coffee, peanuts, and <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Guinea possesses over 25&#160;billion <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">tonnes</a> (metric tons) of bauxite – and perhaps up to one-half of the world's reserves. In addition, Guinea's mineral wealth includes more than 4-billion tonnes of high-grade iron ore, significant diamond and gold deposits, and undetermined quantities of <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>. Guinea has considerable potential for growth in agricultural and fishing sectors. Soil, water, and climatic conditions provide opportunities for large-scale irrigated farming and agro industry. Possibilities for investment and commercial activities exist in all these areas, but Guinea's poorly developed infrastructure and rampant corruption continue to present obstacles to large-scale investment projects.</p>
<p>Joint venture bauxite mining and alumina operations in northwest Guinea historically provide about 80% of Guinea's <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_reserves" title="Foreign exchange reserves" class="mw-redirect">foreign exchange</a>. Bauxite is refined into alumina, which is later <a href="/wiki/Smelting" title="Smelting">smelted</a> into aluminium. The <i>Compagnie des Bauxites de Guinea</i> (CBG), which exports about 14 million tonnes of high-grade bauxite annually, is the main player in the bauxite industry. CBG is a joint venture, 49% owned by the Guinean Government and 51% by an international consortium known as Halco Mining Inc., a joint venture of Dadco Mining and <a href="/wiki/Rio_Tinto_Alcan" title="Rio Tinto Alcan">Rio Tinto Alcan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Compagnie des Bauxites de Kindia</i> (CBK), a joint venture between the Government of Guinea and <a href="/wiki/United_Company_RUSAL" title="United Company RUSAL" class="mw-redirect">RUSAL</a>, produces some 2.5&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">tonnes</a> annually, nearly all of which is exported to <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and Eastern Europe. <a href="/wiki/Dian_Dian" title="Dian Dian">Dian Dian</a>, a Guinean/<a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukrainian</a> joint bauxite venture, has a projected production rate of 1,000,000&#160;<a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">t</a> (1,102,311 <a href="/wiki/Short_ton" title="Short ton">short tons</a>; 984,207 <a href="/wiki/Long_ton" title="Long ton">long tons</a>) per year, but is not expected to begin operations for several years. The <i><a href="/wiki/Alumina_Company_of_Guinea" title="Alumina Company of Guinea">Alumina Compagnie de Guinée</a></i> (ACG), which took over the former Friguia Consortium, produced about 2.4&#160;million tonnes in 2004 as raw material for its alumina refinery. The refinery exports about 750,000 tonnes of alumina. Both Global Alumina and Alcoa-Alcan have signed conventions with the Government of Guinea to build large alumina refineries with a combined capacity of about 4 million tonnes per year.</p>
<p>Diamonds and gold also are mined and exported on a large scale. AREDOR, a joint diamond-mining venture between the Guinean Government (50%) and an Australian, British, and Swiss <a href="/wiki/Consortium" title="Consortium">consortium</a>, began production in 1984 and mined diamonds that are 90% gem quality. Production stopped from 1993 until 1996, when First City Mining, of Canada, purchased the international portion of the consortium. The bulk of diamonds are mined artisanally. The largest gold mining operation in Guinea is a joint venture between the government and <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_Goldfields" title="Ashanti Goldfields" class="mw-redirect">Ashanti Goldfields</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>. Société Minière de Dinguiraye (SMD) also has a large gold mining facility in Lero, near the Malian border.</p>
<p>Guinea has large reserves of the steel-making raw material, iron ore. Rio Tinto is the majority owner of the $6 billion Simandou iron ore project, which the firm says is the world's best unexploited resource.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Rio Tinto has signed a binding agreement with <a href="/wiki/Aluminum_Corp._of_China_Ltd." title="Aluminum Corp. of China Ltd." class="mw-redirect">Aluminum Corp. of China Ltd.</a> to establish the joint venture for the Simandou iron ore project. This project is said to be of the same magnitude as the <a href="/wiki/Pilbara" title="Pilbara">Pilbara</a> in Western Australia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In September 2011, Guinea adopted a new mining code. The law set up a commission to review deals struck during the chaotic days between the end of dictatorship in 2008 and Condé coming to power.<sup id="cite_ref-TST_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TST-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Problems_and_reforms">Problems and reforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Problems and reforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2002, the <a href="/wiki/IMF" title="IMF" class="mw-redirect">IMF</a> suspended Guinea's <a href="/wiki/Poverty_Reduction_and_Growth_Facility" title="Poverty Reduction and Growth Facility">Poverty Reduction and Growth Facility</a> (PRGF) because the government failed to meet key performance criteria. In reviews of the PRGF, the World Bank noted that Guinea had met its spending goals in targeted social priority sectors. However, spending in other areas, primarily defense, contributed to a significant fiscal deficit.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The loss of IMF funds forced the government to finance its debts through <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank" title="Central Bank" class="mw-redirect">Central Bank</a> advances. The pursuit of unsound economic policies has resulted in imbalances that are proving hard to correct.</p>
<p>Under then-Prime Minister Diallo, the government began a rigorous reform agenda in December 2004 designed to return Guinea to a PRGF with the IMF. Exchange rates have been allowed to float, price controls on gasoline have been loosened, and government spending has been reduced while tax collection has been improved. These reforms have not reduced inflation, which hit 27% in 2004 and 30% in 2005. Currency depreciation is also a concern. The Guinea franc was trading at 2550 to the dollar in January 2005. It hit 5554 to the dollar by October 2006.</p>
<p>Despite the opening in 2005 of a new road connecting Guinea and Mali, most major roadways remain in poor repair, slowing the delivery of goods to local markets. Electricity and water shortages are frequent and sustained, and many businesses are forced to use expensive power generators and fuel to stay open.</p>
<p>Even though there are many problems plaguing Guinea's economy, not all foreign investors are reluctant to come to Guinea. Global Alumina's proposed alumina refinery has a price tag above $2&#160;billion. Alcoa and Alcan are proposing a slightly smaller refinery worth about $1.5&#160;billion. Taken together, they represent the largest private investment in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a> since the <a href="/wiki/Chad-Cameroon_Petroleum_Development_and_Pipeline_Project" title="Chad-Cameroon Petroleum Development and Pipeline Project" class="mw-redirect">Chad-Cameroon oil pipeline</a>. Also, Hyperdynamics Corporation, an American oil company, signed an agreement in 2006 to develop Guinea's offshore Senegal Basin oil deposits in a concession of 31,000 square miles (80,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup>); it is pursuing seismic exploration.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 13 October 2009, Guinean Mines Minister Mahmoud Thiam announced that the <a href="/wiki/China_International_Fund" title="China International Fund">China International Fund</a> would invest more than $7bn (£4.5bn) in infrastructure. In return, he said the firm would be a "strategic partner" in all mining projects in the mineral-rich nation. He said the firm would help build ports, railway lines, power plants, low-cost housing and even a new administrative centre in the capital, <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2011, Mohamed Lamine Fofana, the Mines Minister following the <a href="/wiki/Guinean_presidential_election,_2010" title="Guinean presidential election, 2010">2010 election</a>, said that the government had overturned the agreement by the ex-military junta.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcmines_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcmines-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Youth unemployment, however, remains a large problem. Guinea needs an adequate policy to address the concerns of the urban youth. The problem is the disparity between their life and what they see on television. As the youth cannot find jobs, seeing the economic power and consumerism of richer countries only serves to frustrate them further.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil">Oil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Oil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Guinea signed a <a href="/wiki/Production_sharing_agreement" title="Production sharing agreement">Production sharing agreement</a> with Hyperdynamics Corporation of <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a> in 2006 to explore a large offshore tract, recently in partnership with Dana Petroleum PLC (<a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a>, United Kingdom). The initial well, the Sabu-1, was scheduled to begin drilling in October 2011 at a site in approximately 700&#160;meters of water. The Sabu-1 will target a four-way <a href="/wiki/Anticline" title="Anticline">anticline</a> prospect with <a href="/wiki/Upper_Cretaceous" title="Upper Cretaceous" class="mw-redirect">upper Cretaceous</a> sands and is anticipated to be drilled to a total depth of 3,600&#160;meters.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Following the completion of exploratory <a href="/wiki/Drilling" title="Drilling">drilling</a> in 2012, the Sabu-1 well was not deemed commercially viable.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2012, Hyperdynamics subsidiary SCS reached an agreement for a sale of 40% of the concession to <a href="/wiki/Tullow_Oil" title="Tullow Oil">Tullow Oil</a>, bringing ownership shares in the Guinea offshore tract to 37% Hyperdynamics, 40% Tullow Oil, and 23% Dana Petroleum.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> Hyperdynamics will have until September 2016 under the current agreement to begin drilling its' next selected site, the Fatala <a href="/wiki/Turbidite" title="Turbidite">turbidite</a> fan prospect.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_infrastructure">Transport infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Transport infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Guinea" title="Transport in Guinea">Transport in Guinea</a></div>
<p>The railway from Conakry to <a href="/wiki/Kankan" title="Kankan">Kankan</a> ceased operating in the mid-1980s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Domestic air services are intermittent. Most vehicles in Guinea are 20+ years old, and cabs are any four-door vehicle which the owner has designated as being for hire. Locals, nearly entirely without vehicles of their own, rely upon these taxis (which charge per seat) and small buses to take them around town and across the country. There is some river traffic on the Niger and Milo rivers. Horses and donkeys pull carts, primarily to transport construction materials.</p>
<p><br />
Mining operations are expected to start at <a href="/wiki/Simandou" title="Simandou">Simandou</a> before the end of 2015. <a href="/wiki/Rio_Tinto_Limited" title="Rio Tinto Limited" class="mw-redirect">Rio Tinto Limited</a> plans to build a 650&#160;km railway to transport iron ore from the mine to the coast, near <a href="/wiki/Matakong" title="Matakong">Matakong</a>, for export.<sup id="cite_ref-Railways_Africa_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Railways_Africa-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> Much of the Simandou iron ore is expected to be shipped to China for steel production.<sup id="cite_ref-Bulk_Materials_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bulk_Materials-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Conakry_International_Airport" title="Conakry International Airport">Conakry International Airport</a> is the largest airport in the country, with flights to other cities in Africa as well as to Europe.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Guinea" title="Demography of Guinea" class="mw-redirect">Demography of Guinea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pita,_Guinea.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Pita%2C_Guinea.gif/200px-Pita%2C_Guinea.gif" width="200" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Pita%2C_Guinea.gif/300px-Pita%2C_Guinea.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9e/Pita%2C_Guinea.gif 2x" data-file-width="398" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pita,_Guinea.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Guinean women.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The population of Guinea is estimated at 10.5&#160;million. <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>, the capital and largest city, is the hub of Guinea's economy, commerce, education, and culture. In 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> (TFR) of Guinea was estimated at 4.93 children born per woman.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Guinea" title="Languages of Guinea">Languages of Guinea</a></div>
<p>The official language of Guinea is <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>. Other significant languages spoken are <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Pular</a> (Fulfulde or Fulani), <a href="/wiki/Maninka_language" title="Maninka language">Maninka</a> (Malinke), <a href="/wiki/Susu_language" title="Susu language">Susu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kissi_language" title="Kissi language">Kissi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kpelle_language" title="Kpelle language">Kpelle</a>,and <a href="/wiki/Loma_language" title="Loma language">Loma</a>,</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The population of Guinea comprises about 24 ethnic groups. The <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fulas or Fulani</a> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <span lang="fr"><i>Peuls</i></span>; <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Fula</a>: <span lang="ff"><i>Fulɓe</i></span>), comprise 40% of the population and are mostly found in the <a href="/wiki/Futa_Djallon" title="Futa Djallon" class="mw-redirect">Futa Djallon region</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_people" title="Mandinka people">Mandinka</a>, also known as Mandingo or Malinké, comprise 26% of the population and are mostly found in eastern Guinea concentrated around the <a href="/wiki/Kankan_Prefecture" title="Kankan Prefecture">Kankan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kissidougou_Prefecture" title="Kissidougou Prefecture">Kissidougou</a> prefectures.<sup id="cite_ref-guinea_stats_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guinea_stats-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Soussou" title="Soussou" class="mw-redirect">Soussou</a>, comprising 11% of the population, are predominantly in western areas around the capital <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>, <a href="/wiki/For%C3%A9cariah" title="Forécariah">Forécariah</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kindia" title="Kindia">Kindia</a>. Smaller ethnic groups make up the remaining 23% of the population, including <a href="/wiki/Kpelle_people" title="Kpelle people">Kpelle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kissi_people" title="Kissi people">Kissi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zialo" title="Zialo" class="mw-redirect">Zialo</a>, Toma and others.<sup id="cite_ref-guinea_stats_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guinea_stats-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> Approximately 10,000 non-Africans live in Guinea, predominantly Lebanese, French, and other Europeans.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Guinea" title="Religion in Guinea">Religion in Guinea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Conakrymosque.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Conakrymosque.jpg/200px-Conakrymosque.jpg" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Conakrymosque.jpg/300px-Conakrymosque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Conakrymosque.jpg/400px-Conakrymosque.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Conakrymosque.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Conakry_Grand_Mosque" title="Conakry Grand Mosque">Conakry Grand Mosque</a> in Guinea, one of the largest mosques in West Africa.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Guinea is approximately 85 percent Muslim, 8 percent Christian, with 7 percent adhering to indigenous religious beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-state.gov_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state.gov-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> Much of the population, both Muslim and Christian, also incorporate indigenous African beliefs into their outlook.<sup id="cite_ref-state.gov_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state.gov-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Guinean Muslims are generally <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> of <a href="/wiki/Maliki" title="Maliki">Maliki</a> school of jurisprudence, influenced with <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> with many <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyya</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> there are relatively few <a href="/wiki/Shi%27a_Islam" title="Shi'a Islam" class="mw-redirect">Shi'a</a> in Guinea.</p>
<p>Christian groups include <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" title="Roman Catholics" class="mw-redirect">Roman Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventists</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical</a> groups. <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> are active in the country and recognized by the Government. There is a small <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">Baha'i</a> community. There are small numbers of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhists</a>, and traditional Chinese religious groups among the <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriate</a> community.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>There were 3 days of ethno-religious fighting in the city of <a href="/wiki/Nzerekore" title="Nzerekore" class="mw-redirect">Nzerekore</a> in July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Guinea_2013_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guinea_2013-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Fighting between ethnic <a href="/wiki/Kpelle_people" title="Kpelle people">Kpelle</a>, who are Christian or animist, and ethnic Konianke, who are Muslims and close to the larger <a href="/wiki/Malinke" title="Malinke" class="mw-redirect">Malinke</a> ethnic group, left at least 54 dead.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The dead included people who were killed with machetes and burned alive.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The violence ended after the Guinea military imposed a curfew, and President Conde made a televised appeal for calm.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_71-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Guinea" title="Education in Guinea">Education in Guinea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg/220px-Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg" width="220" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg/330px-Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg/440px-Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="489" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_schoolgirls.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Schoolgirls in <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>, Guinea</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The literacy rate of Guinea is one of the lowest in the world: in 2010 it was estimated that only 41% of adults were literate (52% of males and 30% of females).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Primary education is compulsory for 6 years, but most children do not attend for so long, and many do not go to school at all. In 1999, primary school attendance was 40 percent. Children, particularly girls, are kept out of school in order to assist their parents with domestic work or agriculture,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> or to be married: Guinea has one of the highest rates of <a href="/wiki/Child_marriage" title="Child marriage">child marriage</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Guinea" title="Health in Guinea">Health in Guinea</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ebola">Ebola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Ebola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_epidemic_in_West_Africa" title="Ebola virus epidemic in West Africa">Ebola virus epidemic in West Africa</a></div>
<p>In 2014 there was an outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_epidemic_in_Guinea" title="Ebola virus epidemic in Guinea">Ebola virus in Guinea</a>. In response, the health ministry banned <a href="/wiki/Bushmeat" title="Bushmeat">the sale and consumption of bats</a>, thought to be carriers of the disease. Despite this measure, the virus eventually spread from rural areas to <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> and by late June 2014 had spread to neighboring countries <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>. In early August 2014 Guinea closed its borders to Sierra Leone and Liberia to help contain the spreading of the virus, as more new cases of the disease were being reported in those countries than in Guinea. The outbreak began in early December, in a village called Meliandou, southeastern Guinea, not far from the borders with both Liberia and Sierra Leone. The first known case was a two-year-old child who died, after fever and vomiting and passing black stool, on December 6. The child's mother died a week later, then a sister and a grandmother, all with symptoms that included fever, vomiting, and diarrhea. Then, by way of caregiving visits or attendance at funerals, the outbreak spread to other villages.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maternal_and_child_healthcare">Maternal and child healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Maternal and child healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In June 2011, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Population_Fund" title="United Nations Population Fund">United Nations Population Fund</a> released a report on <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.unfpa.org/sowmy/report/home.html">The State of the World's Midwifery</a>. It contained new data on the midwifery workforce and policies relating to newborn and maternal mortality for 58 countries. The 2010 maternal mortality rate per 100,000 births for Guinea is 680. This is compared with 859.9 in 2008 and 964.7 in 1990. The under 5 mortality rate, per 1,000 births is 146 and the neonatal mortality as a percentage of under 5's mortality is 29. In Guinea the number of midwives per 1,000 live births is 1 and the lifetime risk of death for pregnant women is 1 in 26. <sup id="cite_ref-SOWMY_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOWMY-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Guinea has the second highest prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="HIV.2FAIDS">HIV/AIDS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: HIV/AIDS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Guinea" title="HIV/AIDS in Guinea">HIV/AIDS in Guinea</a></div>
<p>An estimated 170,000 adults and children were infected at the end of 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Surveillance surveys conducted in 2001 and 2002 show higher rates of HIV in urban areas than in rural areas. Prevalence was highest in <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a> (5%) and in the cities of the <a href="/wiki/Forest_Guinea" title="Forest Guinea" class="mw-redirect">Forest Guinea</a> region (7%) bordering <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%E2%80%99Ivoire" title="Côte d’Ivoire" class="mw-redirect">Côte d’Ivoire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-usaid_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaid-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>HIV is spread primarily through multiple-partner <a href="/wiki/Heterosexual" title="Heterosexual" class="mw-redirect">heterosexual</a> intercourse. Men and women are at nearly equal risk for HIV, with young people aged 15 to 24 most vulnerable. Surveillance figures from 2001–2002 show high rates among commercial sex workers (42%), active military personnel (6.6%), truck drivers and bush taxi drivers (7.3%), miners (4.7%), and adults with tuberculosis (8.6%).<sup id="cite_ref-usaid_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaid-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Several factors are fueling the HIV/<a href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS" class="mw-redirect">AIDS</a> epidemic in Guinea. They include unprotected sex, multiple sexual partners, illiteracy, endemic poverty, unstable borders, refugee migration, lack of civic responsibility, and scarce medical care and public services.<sup id="cite_ref-usaid_81-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usaid-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malnutrition">Malnutrition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Malnutrition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Malnutrition is a serious problem for Guinea. A 2012 study reported high chronic malnutrition rates, with levels ranging from 34% to 40% by region, as well as acute malnutrition rates above 10% in Upper Guinea’s mining zones. The survey showed that 139,200 children suffer from acute malnutrition, 609,696 from chronic malnutrition and further 1,592,892 suffer from anemia. Degradation of care practices, limited access to medical services, inadequate hygiene practices and a lack of food diversity explain these levels.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaria">Malaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Malaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a> is prevalent in Guinea. It is transmitted year-round, with peak transmission from July through October.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> Malaria is one of the top causes of disability in Guinea.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_Dinguiraye_market.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Guinea_Dinguiraye_market.jpg/300px-Guinea_Dinguiraye_market.jpg" width="300" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/77/Guinea_Dinguiraye_market.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/77/Guinea_Dinguiraye_market.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="293" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guinea_Dinguiraye_market.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A market stall selling vegetables in <a href="/wiki/Dinguiraye_Prefecture" title="Dinguiraye Prefecture">Dinguiraye Prefecture</a>, Guinea.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Polygamy">Polygamy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Polygamy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Polygamy_in_Guinea" title="Polygamy in Guinea">Polygamy in Guinea</a></div>
<p>Polygamy is prohibited by law in Guinea.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> reports that 53.4% of Guinean women aged 15–49 are in polygamous marriages.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Guinea" title="Music of Guinea">Music of Guinea</a></div>
<p>Like other West African countries, Guinea has a rich musical tradition. The group <a href="/wiki/Bembeya_Jazz" title="Bembeya Jazz">Bembeya Jazz</a> became popular in the 1960s after Guinean independence.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Guinea" title="Cuisine of Guinea">Cuisine of Guinea</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Guinean_cuisine" title="Guinean cuisine" class="mw-redirect">Guinean cuisine</a> varies by region with rice as a common staple. Cassava is also widely consumed.<sup id="cite_ref-friends_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-friends-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> Part of <a href="/wiki/West_African_cuisine" title="West African cuisine">West African cuisine</a>, the foods of Guinea include <a href="/wiki/Fufu" title="Fufu">fufu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jollof_rice" title="Jollof rice">jollof rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maafe" title="Maafe">maafe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tapalapa_bread" title="Tapalapa bread">tapalapa bread</a>. In rural areas food is eaten from a large serving dish and eaten by hand outside of homes.<sup id="cite_ref-dc_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dc-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Female_genital_mutilation">Female genital mutilation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Female genital mutilation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-one_source" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="Question book-new.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="262" data-file-height="204" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>relies largely or entirely upon a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">single source</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Guinea#.23" title="Talk:Guinea">talk page</a>. Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Guinea&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by introducing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> to additional sources.</span> <small><i>(November 2014)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>According to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Anastasia_Gage&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Anastasia Gage (page does not exist)">Anastasia Gage</a>, an associate professor at <a href="/wiki/Tulane_University" title="Tulane University">Tulane University</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ronan_van_Rossem&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ronan van Rossem (page does not exist)">Ronan van Rossem</a>, an associate professor at <a href="/wiki/Ghent_University" title="Ghent University">Ghent University</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> female genital mutilation in Guinea had been performed on more than 98% of women as of 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> In Guinea almost all cultures, religions, and ethnicities practice female genital mutilation.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
